text-align: center;\">\n</div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TRWKShlTI6I/AAAAAAAACYA/1rf6AtEUqIs/s1600/dark.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "12", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/5067190153352744372/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "4416238003218366137", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2010-11-20T22:33:00+05:30", "updated": "2010-12-14T14:59:43+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMjkyMzE4OTgzNDIxCm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2010/11/annex-1-closed-cycle-wash-on-chemical.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/4416238003218366137", "title": "ANNEX 1 CLOSED CYCLE WASH ON CHEMICAL TANKERS-- CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TOf-clKefOI/AAAAAAAAAiM/3ZwAlkXPb9E/s1600/PC040084.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"240\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TOf-clKefOI/AAAAAAAAAiM/3ZwAlkXPb9E/s320/PC040084.JPG\" width=\"320\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 16pt;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 16pt;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;ANNEX ONE OILS CLOSED CYCLE WASH<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">A closed cycle wash is a wonderful system where you can wash a ULCC and not discharge a drop of oil into the sea. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Some of the old chemical tankers have a equalizing line between the port and stbd slops . The position of the lower of the two equalizing valves determines which is the clean slop and which is the dirty slop.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">*The lower equalizing valve leads to the bottom of the dirty slop. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">*The upper part of equalizing line leads to the top of the clean slop.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">*The CLEAN water for tankcleaning is drawn from the bottom of the clean slop, where lighter oil droplets cannot exist.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">*The dirty washings stripped continiously from butterworthed tank bottoms are put into the dirty slop from top without creating turbulence.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">To do closed cycle wash first fill up both slops to a suitable level. Prior to this the clean slop has to be washed and washings stripped into the dirty slop of course. Once washing starts a layer of oil will keep building up on top surface of the dirty slop. After butterworthing ensure line flushing is also done into the dirty slop.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Once the washing is over the clean slop is pumped overboard through the ODMCS.&nbsp; The dirty slop is allowed to settle and separate for 24 hours . Heating can hasten the separation. The clean water from below is discharged through the ODMCS. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">As long as the IRD is within 30 litres per nautical mile the overboard will remain open. If the IRD exceeds the discharge will be diverted back to the dirty slop and the overboard will automatically shut. Do not try to overdo the decanting with heavy persistant oils which can dirty the sensor , especially if ship is rolling.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">&nbsp;IRD ( litres per nm )= PPM &nbsp;X &nbsp;flow rate ( CuM per hour ) / speed ( &nbsp;in knots ) &nbsp;X 1000<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">It is obvious that the CCR is not concerned with ppm like the Engine room. To reduce the IRD below 30 litres/ nm either the ships speed can be increased or the flow rate can be reduced by reducing the pump rpm. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The water in the dirty slop is pumped ashore or into a slop barge. After that the tank is butterworthed and that too is discharged as slops.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Some chemical tankers with deepwell pumps do not have an equalizer line between the slops. In such a case use any tank as a dirty slop tank and strip tank washings into it.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">It is important to superstrip cargo lines at end of discharge to reduce the shore tank / barge slop quantity, especially for lub oils<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Some chemical time charterers fix up deck tanks ( endorsed in IOPP certificate ) so that they do not have a Annex one oil slop barge liability in uneconomical ports and to avoid sacrificing the slop tank just to accommodate manifold drip tray oily water and to accommodate incompatible chemical slops.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">No decanting of dirty slop can be done in special areas. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">############</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">ON SS CHEMICAL TANKERS : ( on request from Capt Tajbar Rawat-- via blog on Marpol rules &nbsp;)</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">It is obvious that you have to use fresh water in case of long slop carriage ( chloride pitting on SS ) and your slop tanks will NOT have the closed cycle equalising/ siphoning system.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">You cannot have any tankcleaning chemical mixed with the decanted and retained slop, as nobody will accept this annex 1+2 mix. &nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">There is a huge doubt at sea-- as to how much water must be consumed ( to log in oil record book ) before you can start washing with tank cleaning chemicals and pump the strippings directly overboard, as this is NOT addressed anywhere. &nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Best is to prewash it ashore -- but very few charterers want to spend this money, and very few ports have such facility for huge volumes .&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">You can be assured that as long as your wash water is hot and you treat the annex 1 ( especially persistant viscous lub oils ) as category X annex 2 cargo for Marpol purposes of K value for \" soldifying/ high viscocity substance \" as per P&amp;A manual-- you cannot have a run in with the IGNORANT port state control . &nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Now, how do you use so much water, as you dont have this much tank cleaning fresh water ROB ? &nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Use TWO PASS mode -- where you strip all bottom washings into the SMALL dirty slop tank ( which also takes in the ODMCS reject ) using drop from top, without splashing . &nbsp;On a ULCC &nbsp;you use CONTINIOUS pass mode which may be 10 pass or more-- remember?</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Remember the bottom of this tank must be charged with good clean water to a height of atleast one metre, to keep the framo pump mouth clean &nbsp;--so that when you shift some water for the 2nd pass from dirty slop to the clean slop for wash water drive -- NO oil traces carry. &nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Empty the clean slops fully ( into dirty slop tank ) by consuming for tank wash , before you finally decant the dirty slop via ODMCS. Ensure you enter 1/30000 DWT into the ODMCS CPU as the total weight of lub oils carried during the voyage --it is NOT summer DWT.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p>And with Lub oils dont wait for the overboard to slam shut at 30 litres / nautical mile- by which time your sensor is already dirty. The modern ODMCS units do NOT have sensor cleaning soap/ emulsifier solution -- as this soap foam solution inside the decanted slop can be rejected .&nbsp;</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p><br />\n</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p>Alter course and run the steam coils to keep the oil interface right on the surface of the slop to be decanted.</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p><br />\n</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p>Finally this decanted ROB must be stripped into the deck tank as long as it is in the IOPP certificate form B , so that you do NOT waste a slop cargo tank on a ANNEX 2 chemical tanker. If this deck tank is epoxy coated--you can use salt water for washing instead of fresh water. The deck tank slop content can be carried till you reach an economical port.</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p><br />\n</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p>In the ORB mention that you used 2 pass ,when you use limited fresh water.</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQc5AnlczgI/AAAAAAAAB4M/LCDzzsH732w/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQc5AnlczgI/AAAAAAAAB4M/LCDzzsH732w/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" /></a></div><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p><br />\n</o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">-------CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 YEARS IN COMMAND )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 30.0pt; margin-right: 30.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. font-size: 16pt;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 16pt;\">PHENOL ON CHEMICAL TANKERS<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">During loading operations in cold weather , PHENOL vapour will be released into the atmosphere during loading and can fall as snow and you need a stout heart under your PPE.<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">In the <st1:place w:st=\"on\">Auschwitz</st1:place> concentration during world war II , camp prisoners were exterminated by phenol injections (Abspritzen) straight into the heart. <o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">If Phenol falls on 4 square inches of your skin you may die within 30 minutes to several hours.<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">During the delay there will be gradual damage to kidneys, liver, pancreas, spleen, with edema of lungs. There may be burning pain, pallor, sweating, weakness, dark urine, tremors, twitches, vomitting, ringing in ears, fall of body temp , mental confusion, vertigo and shock. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">It is thus important to reassure the unfortunate casuality, who has not worn proper PPE.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Loading Phenol from barges especially in freezing temperatures is a huge risk. The reason is that the cargo is highly poisonous and can freeze in the pipelines because its MP is 40.6 deg C and cargo solidifies. &nbsp;If you allow the cargo to freeze in the pipelines you expose your crew to Phenol and you have failed in your duty. Any stoppages of cargo due to the barge doing internal stripping , barge change over etc must be known to you. You must remember it is easier to blow by assistance of gravity than against the trim uphill when the nitrogen blow will skim over the cargo and cool and freeze it. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">When trying to blow through and clear the frozen lines&nbsp; SAFETY FIRST is the watchword. Don\u2019t try to save time at the expense of crew safety. Everything must be planned. Before you put your hands into motion put your brain in gear.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">If the pipelines freeze it is easier to apply very hot water (95C) externally especially at bends. Application of steam externally is too local and will take too long. You cannot blow with steam internally as the cargo is moisture sensitive. It is a good idea to have steam copper tubes for thermal tracing of pipelines , especially the manifold common collector. If you cant steam trace the common collector do NOT use it. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Used to manufacture antiseptic, disinfectants, slimicides, mouth wash, sore throat lozenges etc <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Properties:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Old name/ carbolic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Aromatic alcohol<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Clear pink colour<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Sweet sickening tarry odour<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">CHRIS/ PHN<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Marpol category/ Y<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">USCG/ 21<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">MP/ 40.6C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">VP/ 3.07 mm HG @50C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">VD/ 3.24<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">SG/ 1.07<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">BP/ 182C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Visc/ 4mPas @45C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">VH/ 50C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">AH/ 60C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">DH/ 55C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">AIT/ 715C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">FP/ 85C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Flammable limits/ 1.7 to 8.6<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Absorbs water from air<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Soluble in ethanol and ether.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Antidote/ PEG polyethylene glycol (for skin) or 70:30 PEG / methylated spirit mixture swab with cotton.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Combustible<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Nitrogen / yes<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">TLV/ 5 ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Odour threshold/ 1 ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Soluble in water completely at 60C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Surface tension / high-40.9 dynes/ cm @20C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Good cargo if next cargo is WW<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Air and moisture sensitive<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Highly poisonous.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Liquid turns red if not perfectly pure or under influence of light.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Sensitive to sudden heat adjustments, may form tarry deposits and become discoloured.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">When heated emits toxic and irritating fumes.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Corrosive to skin and respiratory tract.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Poisonous through skin contact. Will give severe burns.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Vapors affects nervous system. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Emergency first aid procedures</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Sufficient Drager tubes&nbsp; (order number 81 01641) must be available before PHENOL is loaded. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Neoprene gloves are resistant.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Chemical antidote/ POLYETHYLENE GLYCOL should be swabbed liberally onto the affected area. the emergency shower must be used, with the patient remaining in the shower for at least 5 minutes.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">MSDS sheets must be posted and non-essential personnel must be kept clear of the operating area and taped off. &nbsp;Access to the vessel should be from behind the manifold and all persons must be made aware that PHENOL operations are to be conducted.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Preparation For Loading<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Remove flame screens if fitted , for vapors can condense and solidify.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Prior to arriving in the load port, the tanks to be utilized for the carriage of PHENOL must be cleaned for Water White Standard and its pH must be between 6 and 8. &nbsp;All hose/pipe connections must be pressure tested before commencing any operations to ensure connections are tight. The tank and lines must be dry and odourfree. All joints must be of PTFE and all leaks rectified before commencing cargo operations. Heating coils must be tested and lof entry made. Loading PHENOL is a closed operation. When configuring lines for loading PHENOL, facilities must be available at the manifold to blow nitrogen through all lines used and back into all tanks loaded.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Tanks to be loaded should have ballast removed from underneath and heating coils must be opened once product has fully covered the coils. The PHENOL must be carried at temperatures within charterers instructions, typically between +45 and + 60 degrees centigrade. If cargo is presented at the discharge port at a temperature greater than 10 <sup>o</sup>C above the freezing point, then there will be no need to undertake pre-washing . A full cargo heating log must be maintained.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The fire main must be pressurized throughout, with monitors/hoses ready at all times.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Restrict personnel on deck.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Loading </span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Once loading has commenced, it must not be interrupted unless absolutely essential. If&nbsp; loading is interrupted, lines must be blown immediately. Rates to individual tanks should be adjusted to facilitate quick and effective topping off, without risk to personnel.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Venting</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">As PHENOL freezes at +40<sup>o</sup>C, personnel must be aware that there is a possibility that vent lines may become blocked should the vapour freeze. During loading operations, PHENOL vapour will be released into the atmosphere during loading and can fall as snow. Depending on wind direction and strength, there will always be a real risk that PHENOL may be deposited over a large area of the vessel.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Topping Off</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Wherever possible, tanks being loaded must be topped off&nbsp; as quickly as possible in sequence to prevent lines freezing. Loading rates to each tank must be adjusted to minimize the chances of product freezing in the lines before they can be blown. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Line Blowing<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">If lines have to be blown uphill it is better to steam trace the lines in freezing weather.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">A major factor in safe and efficient PHENOL operations is the correct and effective blowing of cargo lines upon completion of loading. &nbsp;High pressure nitrogen must be prepared well in advance of anticipated need. Once tanks have been loaded, manifold valves should be shut and the nitrogen line connected. The nitrogen supply should be opened and pressure allowed to build up. At no time should pressure exceed the safe working pressure of flexible hoses/pipes. Once a sufficient pressure (typically&nbsp; &gt;7 bar) has been achieved,&nbsp; the manifold valve for the line to be blown should be slowly opened until the nitrogen starts to move into the line. The manifold valve must not be opened any further. The noise of the high pressure nitrogen should be heard, along with the sound of the liquid phenol, being forced back into the tank. The manifold valve should not be opened fully. Once the pressure has been released, the manifold valve should be closed and the process resumed. This controlled blowing must be conducted until the line to the tank is free from PHENOL. It may well take some 10/15 minutes of blowing each line until the chief officer is completely satisfied that the line are clear. The lines can be tapped using a small hammer or spanner. If a clear bell type ring is heard, then the lines should be clear. A dull \u201cthud\u201d indicates that Phenol is in the line and may already be frozen. &nbsp;Note, the opposite side (of manifold crossover) to loading connection will be solidified and must be externally heated.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Carriage and heating</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Once the lines have been blown, hoses can be disconnected and blanked. During the loaded voyage, flexible hoses should be disconnected and steamed, along with \u201cY\u201d pieces and reducers.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">If no specific heating instructions are supplied, the cargo should be kept at a temperature of approximately +55<sup>o</sup>C, or advice sought from the office.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The PHENOL must be carried at temperatures within charterers instructions, typically between +50 and + 60 degrees centigrade. If cargo is presented at the discharge port at a temperature greater than 10 <sup>o</sup>C above the MP, then there will be no need to undertake pre-washing . &nbsp;A cargo heating log must be maintained.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Normally Phenol heating is carried out by means of thermal oil ( to avoid toxic chemical entering the boiler ) or hot water heating with max inlet temperature of 80 </span><span style=\"font-family: Symbol;\">\u00b0</span><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">C. If vessel is not equipped with thermal oil heating system, the steam heating system is to be re-arranged in order to heat the cargo by hot water without send the return steam back to the engine room hotwell. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">ENSURE THAT THE COILS CONTAIN ONLY WATER BY KEEPING THE COIL INLET VALVE FULLY OPEN AND ADJUSTING THE RETURN VALVE TO CONTROL HEAT OF WATER IN THE COILS. THE RETURN WATER MUST BE SENT TO ANOTHER DEDICATED TOXIC CHECK FW TANK. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Arrangement--<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">fresh water tank \u2013 butterworth pump \u2013 butterworth heater \u2013 steam inlet line- &nbsp;&nbsp;heating coils via portable manifold &nbsp;\u2013 steam return line \u2013 back into the same fresh water tank.<o:p></o:p></span></i></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Preparation for Discharge</span></b><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Prior to arrival at the discharge port, the tanks should be configured for effective discharge, again ensuring that adequate blowing points are available. All connections must be pressure tested for leaks and should any be found, the leaks rectified and the system integrity proven. Complete protective clothing is again required, as it is for all PHENOL operations. As a product, phenol requires closed loading/discharging.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Before commencing discharge, the receivers, or their representative must ensure that adequate&nbsp; tank space is available for the complete cargo. Purge framo pump cofferdam. Once discharge has commenced, the vessel should discharge all tanks without stopping. It should be remembered that, given its high freezing point (+40<sup>o</sup>C), every effort should be made to ensure that tanks are completed as close together as practical/possible, to reduce the chance of product freezing in the lines, before air can be used to clear the lines back to the tanks. Ullages and individual tank rates must be monitored at frequent intervals, with pump speeds adjusted as necessary.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Discharging</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Due to its high freezing point, vapour lines, pressure/vacuum valves, pumpstack valves and deck tank sumps etc. may be blocked due to frozen product. Care must be taken during the initial stages of discharge to ensure that all are unblocked by applying either external live steam or hot water and then;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Product is moving and being discharged. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Tank ventilation is effective for the discharge rate. If there is any doubt, the discharge rate should be slowed down. If discharge has to be stopped, then as mentioned dry air or nitrogen must be available immediately to blow and clear lines.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The fire main is to be pressurized before commencing discharge and throughout all cargo/tank cleaning operations. The anchor cables can be used to bleed pressure, whilst the system is in standby. Foam/water cannons are to be directed over the cargo handling/ manifold area throughout the operation.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">If the cargo is to be discharged in parcels, then the following precautions must be made, prior to completing a parcel.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Nitrogen&nbsp; must be available to immediately blow all lines back to the tank(s) being discharged. Lines must be blown until the Chief officer is satisfied that the lines are clear.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Upon completion of a tank/cargo, a tank dry certificate must be issued immediately, due notice must be given to the receiver\u2019s representative to ensure that he/she is on board and in position prior to completion of cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The minimum number of tanks and lines to be used for each parcel.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Once the tank dry certificate has been issued, lines must be blown until the chief officer is completely satisfied that the lines are clear. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">DURING LINE BLOWING OPERATIONS, ALL NON ESSENTIAL PERSONNEL SHOULD BE PROHIBITED FROM ACCESS TO THE DECK AND ALL PERSONNEL ENGAGED IN PHENOL OPERATIONS MUST WEAR FULL PROTECTIVE CLOTHING AT ALL TIMES. IT SHOULD BE REMEMBERED THAT DURING LINE BLOWING, PHENOL CAN BE BLOWN INTO THE AIR, WITH THE RESULT THAT IT WILL FALL AS SNOW. EXTREME CARE MUST BE TAKEN AT ALL TIMES. Upon completion of blowing, the immediate area should be drenched with sea water to wash away any residual product that may remain.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Water should be introduced in to the empty tank as soon as possible to sufficiently cover the heating coils. This can be done by either using a fire hose&nbsp; (WITHOUT A NOZZLE) or a butterworth machine (WITHOUT A TANK WASHING MACHINE). Once the water is in the tanks and covering the coils, the coils are to be opened. This will have two effects.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Any ROB will be diluted to commence reducing the adverse effects of the cargo and to reduce it\u2019s freezing point.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">The diluted product will be heated to avoid any freezing of pump sumps and lines, which will enable tank cleaning operations to be carried out.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">EXTREME CARE <u>MUST</u> BE TAKEN WHEN OPENING <u>ANY ACCESS</u> TO A TANK WHICH HAS HELD PHENOL. &nbsp;ALL PERSONNEL ENGAGED IN PHENOL OPERATIONS MUST AT ALL TIMES WEAR FULL PROTECTION.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">*N.B./ It has been reported that an exposed area of less than 2 square inches can be fatal!<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Should there be a major leakage, the area should be drenched by using the water cannon. Shore Authorities should be advised if a major spillage occurs.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Pre-Washing</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">PHENOL is a category \u201cY\u201d substance and not to be pre-washed as long as the dischg heat is greater than MP+10C.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Procedures for pre-washing are as follows.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">On completion of discharge, tank dry certificate to be issued by receivers.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Water washing temperature to be at least +60</span><span style=\"font-family: Symbol;\">\u00b0</span><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">C. (PHENOL becomes&nbsp; miscible in water at +60</span><span style=\"font-family: Symbol;\">\u00b0</span><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">C). &nbsp;Use water as per P&amp;A manual. USE FW.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Washings to be transferred to shore reception facilities. (Pre-washing slops can be transferred to a nominated<b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><u> temporary</u></b> slop tank whilst reception facilities are being prepared).<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Once pre-washing has been completed, the Cargo Record Book must be endorsed properly, or a certificate&nbsp; attached to the relevant page.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Tank Cleaning</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Use hot sea water at 75C for two hours.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Fresh water rinse <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">One hour of steaming.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Vent, mop and dry.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Blow all heating coils.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">A tank entry certificate must be completed before any entry into a cargo tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">Phenol will form crystals in vent stacks and PV valves, steam it away.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\">CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 YEARS IN COMMAND )<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">..</span></b>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "6", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/5155992049812161662/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "2878800617870848651", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2010-11-19T22:43:00+05:30", "updated": "2017-12-26T18:56:25+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxNTE0Mjk0Nzg1MDgzCm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2010/11/phosphoric-acid-on-chemical-tankers.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/2878800617870848651", "title": "PHOSPHORIC ACID ON CHEMICAL TANKERS-- CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TOawJnvzcYI/AAAAAAAAAg8/XUMxWq1wwEg/s1600/DSC07863.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"240\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TOawJnvzcYI/AAAAAAAAAg8/XUMxWq1wwEg/s320/DSC07863.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;calibri&quot; , sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;calibri&quot; , sans-serif;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;calibri&quot; , sans-serif;\"></span><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;calibri&quot; , sans-serif; font-size: 16pt;\">PHOSPHORIC ACID ON CHEMICAL TANKERS</span></b><br />\n<b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;calibri&quot; , sans-serif; font-size: 16pt;\"><br />\n</span></b></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQHe49E2FvI/AAAAAAAABo0/DkSc1nrCjQM/s1600/phosphoric.jpg.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQHe49E2FvI/AAAAAAAABo0/DkSc1nrCjQM/s1600/phosphoric.jpg.png\" /></a></div>\n<pre style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;calibri&quot; , sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></pre>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-top: 10.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-align: justify; text-autospace: none;\">\n<b><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Company policy requires ships SS tanks to be passivated after carriage of WET Phosphoric acid.<o:p></o:p></span></b></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-top: 10.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-align: justify; text-autospace: none;\">\n<b><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">The corrosion to austenitic SS of SUS 316L and 316LN occurring due to carriage of wet process phosphoric acid is a very complex phenomenon. White Phosphoric acid (pure food grade) is not corrosive to stainless steel, however, the Wet PAC (fertilizer grade\u2014green PAC and BK PAC &nbsp;) is perhaps the most aggressive and difficult of all chemicals transported in a SS chemical tanker. The corrosion is affected by various impurities normally present in wet process acid. &nbsp;Only 317LN can be said to resist this acid without too much damage and that too if the loading temperatures are within limits..<span style=\"color: black;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></b></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Names: Green phosphoric acid, Bk phosphoric acid, Metaphosphoric acid; Orthophosphoric acid. MARPOL / Z<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-top: 10.0pt; text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">The corrosivity of&nbsp; crude phosphoric acid depends on the manufacturing process\u2014wet or dry. In the wet process the <span style=\"background-color: white;\">Chlorides and Fluorides </span>determine the corrosivity as they are corrosion accelerators.. The amount of Flourides and Chlorides differs from country to country where the raw stock comes from. Wet phosphoric acid must be constantly recirc during the voyage to prevents sediments from depositing. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-top: 10.0pt; text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Even if the ship is carring the same product again the tanks must be cleaned and desedimentised. The green phosphoric acid from <st1:city w:st=\"on\"><st1:place w:st=\"on\">Ashdod</st1:place></st1:city> <st1:country-region w:st=\"on\"><st1:place w:st=\"on\">Israel</st1:place></st1:country-region> does not hold any sediments and hence need not be recirc, &nbsp;however the rest of the worlds fertilizer grade has lot of abrasive sediments. Do not load Phosphoric acid ( wet, fertilizer grade ) in tanks without diffusers.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Reducing acids and very high chloride solutions are unsuitable for carriage in SS tanks. During the production of wet Phosphoric acid, natural Phosphate rock is attacked and dissolved in Sulphuric acid. The Phosphate rock contains impurities that are carried through the process into the product acid. The surplus reducing Sulphuric acid and the impurities cause the corrosion in SS<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Standard compositions:<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">P2O5\u201453.3%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">H2SO4/ 4% ( corrosion accelerator ) <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">SiO2/ 0.4% ( corrosion inhibitor )<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">MgO/ 0.7%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">CaO/ 0.4%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Al2O3/ 1.2%( C inh )<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Fe2O3/ 0.8% ( C inh )<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-top: 9.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-align: justify; text-autospace: none;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">In some cases the cargo acid may be loaded at temperatures grater than ambient. Depending upon the origin this can have an adverse effect on the stainless steel. It is important the Chemical Operator is consulted before loading any Phosphoric Acid that is over 40C. If the temperature of the acid is exceeding 50C the cargo will normally not be loaded.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Before loading consult the SS manufacturers graph for Flourides and Chlorides versus temperature \u2013included &nbsp;in your SS resistance tables given by the yard.&nbsp; Aggressiveness of wet phosphoric acid increases with temperature . Higher temp requires a higher inhibitor content or lower accelerator content. An acid than can be safely carried at 35 deg C will cause corrosion at 45 deg C.&nbsp; Grades 316LN 317LN and 2205 (UNS S31803) --with high nitrogen content are suitable. 317LN can carry higher temps than 316LN. find out from shipper all specs incl temp and the number of days of carriage. When changing shore tanks or loading from wagons\u2014be aware of temp differences.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">ABCD of WET PAC corrosivity--<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">A)Conc P2O5 &lt;54%<o:p></o:p></span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">B)Conc SO4&lt;4%<o:p></o:p></span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">C)Conc CL&lt;200 ppm<o:p></o:p></span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">D)Temp 45 deg C.<o:p></o:p></span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Excess of any two of above items will damage the tank<o:p></o:p></span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Al and Ferric ions are corrosion inhibitors. Calcium , Magnesium and Sodium are secondary inhibitors. Insoluble silica forms the sediments. In case SS corrodes send the samples from each tank&nbsp; to a independent lab to find out the true specs. The conditions under the sediment layer will be more aggressive than the liquid itself. Prewash with FW \u2013first and last with FW.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<b><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Physical Properties</span></b><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Clear, syrupy liquid<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Practically odorless<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">1.64<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Inorganic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">CHRIS/ PAC<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">USCG / Group 1<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">BP/ 135C<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Marpol cat/ Z<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">MP/5 (80% concentration). -- fertilizer grade <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; The dynamic aspect of matter arises in quantum theory as a consequence of the wave-nature of subatomic particles.<br />\n<br />\nTalking about the Quantum Physics we stumbled upon the most bizarre result of quantum theory came when Bell\u2019s theorem and subsequent experiments proved the so called entanglements to be right. In such cases, two or more atoms, electrons or photons demonstrate correlated properties even at distances where no communication is possible between them during the given time.<br />\n<br />\nThese developments are the most important developments in the history of physics and perhaps in the whole of science. Ajit Vadakayil</a></cite><span class=\"icon user blog-author\" style=\"background-image: url(&quot;data:image/png; background-repeat: no-repeat; display: inline-block; font-weight: bold; height: 18px; margin: 0px 0px -4px 6px; width: 18px;\"></span><span class=\"datetime secondary-text\" style=\"margin-left: 6px;\"><a href=\"https://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2017/12/comments-overflow-for-inoperative-load_30.html?showComment=1514595161341#c2849351715198825203\" rel=\"nofollow\" style=\"color: #888888;\">December 30, 2017 at 6:22 AM</a></span></div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" id=\"bc_0_7MC\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px; text-align: justify;\">\nCONTINUED FROM 2-<br />\n<br />\nEntanglement involves putting objects in the peculiar limbo of quantum superposition, in which an object's quantum properties occupy multiple states at once<br />\n<br />\n<span style=\"color: red;\">http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.in/2011/02/schrodinger-father-of-quantum-physics.html</span><br />\n<br />\nPhysicists have entangled particles such as electrons and photons, as well as larger objects such as superconducting electric circuits.<br />\n<br />\nTheoretically, even if entangled objects are separated, their precarious quantum states should remain linked until one of them is measured or disturbed. That measurement instantly determines the state of the other object, no matter how far away. The idea is so counterintuitive that IDIOT Albert Einstein mocked it as \"spooky action at a distance.\"<br />\n<br />\nIn 2015, the most sophisticated of these tests, which involved measuring entangled electrons 1.3 kilometers apart, showed once again that spooky action is real.<br />\n<br />\nBeyond the fundamental result, such experiments also point to the possibility of hack-proof communications.<br />\n<br />\nLong strings of entangled photons, shared between distant locations, can be \"quantum keys\" that secure communications. Anyone trying to eavesdrop on a quantum-encrypted message would disrupt the shared key, alerting everyone to a compromised channel.<br />\n<br />\nPSSSSTTT-- BEFORE CHINA INVENTS THE QUANTUM SATELLITE--WE MUST BREAK THE NATION INTO 4 PARTS AND HAVE TIBET AS A NEIGHBOUR<br />\n<br />\n<br />\nEntangled photons degrade rapidly as they pass through the air or optical fibers. The satellite is the foundation of the $100 million Quantum Experiments at Space Scale program<br />\n<br />\nBell's theorem is a \"no-go theorem\" that draws an important distinction between quantum mechanics (QM) and the world as described by classical mechanics<br />\n<br />\nIn its simplest form, Bell's theorem states: No physical theory of local hidden variables can ever reproduce all of the predictions of quantum mechanics.<br />\n<br />\nBell's theorem is the most profound discovery of science.and it is lifted straight out of the Vedas<br />\n<br />\nThere is no need for a faster-than-light signal to tell particle A what measurement has been carried out on particle B, because the universe, including particle A, already 'knows' what that measurement, and its outcome, will be.<br />\n<br />\nLOT OF MY DETRACTORS WERE GUFFAWING LIKE DONKEY WHO HAVE SEEN FRESH SHIT WHEN THEY HEARD THAT MY WIFE MATCHED MORE THAN 500 HOROSCOPES FOR MY ELDER SONs BRIDE<br />\n<br />\nBell\u2019s theorem and subsequent experiments proved the so called entanglements to be right. In such cases, two or more atoms, electrons or photons demonstrate correlated properties even at distances where no communication is possible between them during the given time.<br />\n<br />\nThese developments are the most important developments in the history of physics and the whole of science. The crystal emitted pairs of photons entangled so that their polarization states would be opposite when one was measured.<br />\n<br />\nThe pairs were split, with photons sent to separate receiving stations in Delingha and Lijiang, 1200 kilometers apart.
